<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17569802883720057841">`Cranford is in possession of the Amazons; all the holders of houses, above a certain rent, are women.' In this witty and poignant comedy of early-Victorian life in a country town, Elizabeth Gaskell describes the uneventful lives of the lady-like inhabitants so as to offer an ironic commentary on the diverse experiences of men and women. She explores the unlikely juxtaposi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17569802883720057841">`Cranford is in possession of the Amazons; all the holders of houses, above a certain rent, are women.' In this witty and poignant comedy of early-Victorian life in a country town, Elizabeth Gaskell describes the uneventful lives of the lady-like inhabitants so as to offer an ironic commentary on the diverse experiences of men and women. She explores the unlikely juxtapositions of old and new brought about by the pace of change: the effects of Victorian commerce and imperial expansion co-exist with the survival of customs and habits of thought from much earlier times. This edition has detailed notes and a new introduction which discusses the originality and subtlety of the book's angle on women's experience.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17569802883720057841">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/215879419?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4012541-sunday" class="user" title="Sunday">Sunday</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer215879419">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18081435747418265848"><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360078ra/710983.gif" /><br /><br />HOW I LOVED THIS BOOK. I've started drinking nothing but tea with a little cream and sugar at this point. So well written and adorable. But tapered with this sadly nostalgic idea that the cottage-and-lace England was fading away into something that ran on steam and could carry a million pounds of cotton. (I'm talking about a train here.) This book was a goddamn joy to read, I tell you, a goddamn DELIGHT.<br /><br />Miss Matty was an ideal-ideal character. Layered like a 10-layer coconut cake on a Food Netwo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18081435747418265848"><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360078ra/710983.gif" /><br /><br />HOW I LOVED THIS BOOK. I've started drinking nothing but tea with a little cream and sugar at this point. So well written and adorable. But tapered with this sadly nostalgic idea that the cottage-and-lace England was fading away into something that ran on steam and could carry a million pounds of cotton. (I'm talking about a train here.) This book was a goddamn joy to read, I tell you, a goddamn DELIGHT.<br /><br />Miss Matty was an ideal-ideal character. Layered like a 10-layer coconut cake on a Food Network showdown. No one can read the little tales about Cranford and their tragedies and joys and not feel twitterpaited. NO ONE. It's a perfect little lace-trimmed window into the soul of a town trapped in a very particular era, with a very particular state of mind. <br /><br />I have a good mind to look through every review less than three-stars on here and troll them until they delete their account and decide perhaps the Sahara desert (sans internet) would be a better place to live. CHECK YOSELF. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=britain" class="actionLinkLite">britain</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1138916247">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11915105407408338222">"the humor is so sly. at times it's difficult to believe that this was written over 150 years ago. I guess that gentle social humor has always been with us." --- this was one of my status updates while reading Cranford, my first experience reading Elizabeth Gaskell. <br /><br />As I finished reading, I felt the same way: pleased with the experience, surprised at the wit and wisdom written so well so many years ago. But then I ask myself...Why am I surprised? There are always intelligent women and always int</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11915105407408338222">"the humor is so sly. at times it's difficult to believe that this was written over 150 years ago. I guess that gentle social humor has always been with us." --- this was one of my status updates while reading Cranford, my first experience reading Elizabeth Gaskell. <br /><br />As I finished reading, I felt the same way: pleased with the experience, surprised at the wit and wisdom written so well so many years ago. But then I ask myself...Why am I surprised? There are always intelligent women and always intelligent women who find ways to make themselves heard even in less than enthusiastic societies. I need to keep looking for them!<br /><br />I had planned to include some of the truly wonderful quotes from various characters but instead I challenge you to read this book and discover them for yourself. I venture to say you will be glad you did.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_900163192">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900163192" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4636758-vanessa" class="left imgcol" title="Vanessa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1366468327p2/4636758.jpg" alt="Vanessa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/900163192?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4636758-vanessa" class="user" title="Vanessa">Vanessa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15827057-cranford" title="Paperback 9780141199429" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4636758-vanessa?shelf=received-as-presents" class="actionLinkLite">received-as-presents</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4636758-vanessa?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer900163192">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9061693409954138877">FINALLY, an Elizabeth Gaskell book that I enjoyed!<br /><br />I honestly didn't think I would enjoy this book, and was almost regretting putting it on my Dewey's 24-Hour Readathon TBR. And whaddya know, I finished it! <br /><br /><em>Cranford</em> follows a group of women living in the small fictional town of, you guessed it, Cranford. The women live in "genteel poverty" and have very old-fashioned mindsets about life and social niceties and norms. The book is told from the perspective of Mary Smith (or Elizabeth Gaskell), and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9061693409954138877">FINALLY, an Elizabeth Gaskell book that I enjoyed!<br /><br />I honestly didn't think I would enjoy this book, and was almost regretting putting it on my Dewey's 24-Hour Readathon TBR. And whaddya know, I finished it! <br /><br /><em>Cranford</em> follows a group of women living in the small fictional town of, you guessed it, Cranford. The women live in "genteel poverty" and have very old-fashioned mindsets about life and social niceties and norms. The book is told from the perspective of Mary Smith (or Elizabeth Gaskell), and focuses mainly on Miss Matty, a sweet-tempered older woman who is one of the pillars of society since the death of her older, revered sister Deborah Jenkyns.<br /><br />This book was cute and sweet and quite funny, which did surprise me. Although it took a little while for me to get used to the language (haven't read a classic in a while, and I usually find Gaskell's writing a little long-winded), it ended up becoming a much easier read than I anticipated. Once you are familiar with the cast of characters and their personalities, it is really enjoyable seeing what will happen to them next.<br /><br />If you're a fan of Gaskell, or even not a fan of Gaskell, I'd definitely recommend it. I'm glad I didn't give up on her writing. Who knows, maybe I'll read another of her books at some point!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9061693409954138877">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_340200216">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/340200216" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4542979-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451622200p2/4542979.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/340200216?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 06, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4542979-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2184302.Cranford" title="Audiobook 9789626348505" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer340200216">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11473660774232305358"><br />What a gorgeous book. After years of avoiding Victorian literature, in the past twelve months I've fallen in love with Gaskell's writing. This is a short work: more a series of episodes than a linear narrative. It centres on the lives of a group of women who dominate society in the small town of Cranford. They are united by being single - widows and spinsters - and by the fact that live in genteel poverty. <br /><br /><em>Cranford</em> is at times laugh-out-loud funny, at times deeply moving. Within five minutes of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11473660774232305358"><br />What a gorgeous book. After years of avoiding Victorian literature, in the past twelve months I've fallen in love with Gaskell's writing. This is a short work: more a series of episodes than a linear narrative. It centres on the lives of a group of women who dominate society in the small town of Cranford. They are united by being single - widows and spinsters - and by the fact that live in genteel poverty. <br /><br /><em>Cranford</em> is at times laugh-out-loud funny, at times deeply moving. Within five minutes of starting the novel I was laughing at the gentle satire on human foibles and life in a small town. Forty minutes later, I was crying about the death of one of the characters. The pattern of alternating laughter and tears continued until the very end. At least, the tears don't last quite till the end: it's a book which thankfully ends on a happy note. <em>Cranford</em> is sentimental, but not cloyingly so. The humour cuts through the sentiment, while making the sad moments even more poignant. <br /><br />The novel is a first person narrative in the form of a memoir. Relatively little is revealed about the narrator, although more becomes known about her as the novel progresses. The narrator is herself a lovely character, although the real star of the novel is the wonderful Miss Matty Jenkyns. I love Miss Matty and I loved spending time in Cranford. I'm particularly happy to have listened to the Naxos audiobook version, superbly narrated by Clare Wille. Now I have to watch the BBC television series and see how it measures up to the original. This is a 4-1/2 star read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11473660774232305358">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_21642240">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21642240" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/250817-inder" class="left imgcol" title="Inder"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1195511213p2/250817.jpg" alt="Inder" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/21642240?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 14, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/250817-inder" class="user" title="Inder">Inder</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/250817-inder?shelf=19th-century" class="actionLinkLite">19th-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250817-inder?shelf=1001-books" class="actionLinkLite">1001-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250817-inder?shelf=read-2008" class="actionLinkLite">read-2008</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250817-inder?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/250817-inder?shelf=england" class="actionLinkLite">england</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer21642240">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9852595766183307003">Ah, so delightful! I <em>loved</em> this. It's really a series of vignettes, and, if there is a plot at all, it doesn't show up until halfway through. But it's so funny! And sad! And it's all about women! I laughed aloud a few times, and almost cried a few other times. <br /><br /><em>Sigh.</em> I'm such a sucker for this stuff. But I loved it. Despite its disjunctive narrative, I read the whole book in less than three days. But I'm strange that way.<br /><br />For Happy (I would alert readers to spoilers, but there actually isn't much</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9852595766183307003">Ah, so delightful! I <em>loved</em> this. It's really a series of vignettes, and, if there is a plot at all, it doesn't show up until halfway through. But it's so funny! And sad! And it's all about women! I laughed aloud a few times, and almost cried a few other times. <br /><br /><em>Sigh.</em> I'm such a sucker for this stuff. But I loved it. Despite its disjunctive narrative, I read the whole book in less than three days. But I'm strange that way.<br /><br />For Happy (I would alert readers to spoilers, but there actually isn't much to spoil):<br /><br />Yeah, the makers of the <em>Masterpiece</em> adaptation took some serious liberties with the plot (or lack thereof). The series is fun and I'm really enjoying it, but it contains several plot lines that are not in the book. In fact, arguably the most important plot lines in the series are completely made up (as opposed to completely made up by Gaskell, I guess). For example, the young doctor and his girl, and all the associated story-lines, simply do not exist in the book. The carpenter with the broken bones - it's all made up. (That disappointed me, because, ever since <em>Middlemarch</em>, I've had a soft spot for young, ambitious doctors in 19th Century English villages. Alas, it was not to be found.) The cute kid who wants to rise above his station? Not only isn't he in the book, but I think the entire idea of him is alien to this novella, which (unlike Gaskell's other work) is centered entirely around the middle and aristocratic classes (and shifts therein), and barely touches on the working class at all.<br /><br />More mildly, all of the timing is wrong (understandable, since following the vignettes too closely would result in a almost cliff-hanger free show, not good TV). And they skip a couple of deaths. There are a surprising number of deaths in this short novella, and I can see that if the series were more faithful to the book, it might be just too depressing. The book is never depressing, although it has sad moments, because of the quality of the narration, but this is difficult to reproduce on film.<br /><br />Overall, there are probably more inconsistencies than similarities between the two. But it's hard to blame the screen-writer - the book doesn't offer much in the way of actual action to work with, and is noticeably missing any love affairs between attractive young people, which, let's face it, is the bread and butter of <em>Masterpiece</em>. The droll, sarcastic, disjunctive narration of commonplace events, makes for a particularly difficult adaptation.<br /><br />But I love it - a new favorite narrator for me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9852595766183307003">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/115473-siria" class="user" title="Siria">Siria</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48142231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6234351774940241145">Beautifully observed and gently funny, <em>Cranford</em> is less a novel than it is a series of vignettes, drawn from the lives of a small group of genteelly impoverished older women in a small town in mid-nineteenth century England. Gaskell is quite gentle with her characters, I think perhaps because she was aware of how limited a life she was creating for them—with all the social restrictions placed on unmarried women, with just enough social status to be unable to work to support themselves, but with</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6234351774940241145">Beautifully observed and gently funny, <em>Cranford</em> is less a novel than it is a series of vignettes, drawn from the lives of a small group of genteelly impoverished older women in a small town in mid-nineteenth century England. Gaskell is quite gentle with her characters, I think perhaps because she was aware of how limited a life she was creating for them—with all the social restrictions placed on unmarried women, with just enough social status to be unable to work to support themselves, but with not enough income to keep themselves independent—and so while they have to face trials, Miss Matty and Co. have the strength and the resilience to face them.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6234351774940241145">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/41518586?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1719730-laurel-hicks" class="user" title="Laurel Hicks">Laurel Hicks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1719730-laurel-hicks?shelf=books-read-in-2008" class="actionLinkLite">books-read-in-2008</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41518586">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2226198682511780049">Great fun! Mrs. Gaskell's gentle yet probing comedy of manners is a book worthy of many readings. There's a lot of dressing up in this book--wearing the perfect hat for the occasion, buying the latest material, dressing a cow in flannel, Peter's ill-received jokes. No clear plot, but then I don't usually read for the plots. The character studies here are priceless.</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_511559797">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/511559797" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7672661-lois-bujold" class="left imgcol" title="Lois Bujold"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442449462p2/7672661.jpg" alt="Lois Bujold" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/511559797?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7672661-lois-bujold" class="user" title="Lois Bujold">Lois Bujold</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer511559797">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11724539507435685239">I picked this up due to a review by Jo Walton on Tor.com. She described it as something like a mid-19th Century English Lake Wobegone, which gives a tolerably accurate sense of the discursive tone. Charming and kindly, with only a tenuous thread of anything one might call a plot, but nonetheless absorbing. I quite liked it. It is available as a free e-edition on Amazon Kindle.<br /><br />The first-person voice makes it very naturally a "told" story, untouched by the later cinematic techniques that infiltrat</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11724539507435685239">I picked this up due to a review by Jo Walton on Tor.com. She described it as something like a mid-19th Century English Lake Wobegone, which gives a tolerably accurate sense of the discursive tone. Charming and kindly, with only a tenuous thread of anything one might call a plot, but nonetheless absorbing. I quite liked it. It is available as a free e-edition on Amazon Kindle.<br /><br />The first-person voice makes it very naturally a "told" story, untouched by the later cinematic techniques that infiltrated narratives in the century following. This also can be a subtly dense style, with a power to pack a lot into a little space. Strong sense of a time and place grown increasingly alien to us. <br /><br />So <em>nice</em> to read something that isn't trying to out-horrific all the others in some mad race for the bottom, even though the story was not untouched by death. The characters' vices were all petty ones, but their virtues, though gentle, were not. I'd almost forgotten books like this could exist. Maybe they can't, anymore.<br /><br />Ta, L.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1209218176">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1209218176" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4971204-katherine" class="left imgcol" title="Katherine"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1418226346p2/4971204.jpg" alt="Katherine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1209218176?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4971204-katherine" class="user" title="Katherine">Katherine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15827057-cranford" title="Paperback 9780141199429" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4971204-katherine?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4971204-katherine?shelf=19th-century" class="actionLinkLite">19th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1209218176">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18255308311902001354">At first, <em>Cranford</em> may seem superficially quaint in it's manner, as it relates the story of a small country town made up of mostly middle-aged women. But to read it only for it's quaintness is to do yourself a disservice, for there is more strength to this novel than just that. <br /><br />The first thing I noticed while reading was the surprisingly modern humor to be picked up on. From forcing laxatives on a fine lace eating cat, to dolling over a cow loved as a daughter (my examples may all be animal rela</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18255308311902001354">At first, <em>Cranford</em> may seem superficially quaint in it's manner, as it relates the story of a small country town made up of mostly middle-aged women. But to read it only for it's quaintness is to do yourself a disservice, for there is more strength to this novel than just that. <br /><br />The first thing I noticed while reading was the surprisingly modern humor to be picked up on. From forcing laxatives on a fine lace eating cat, to dolling over a cow loved as a daughter (my examples may all be animal related, but there's much more), Cranford's society is absolutely hilarious. But the integrity isn't lacking either. Each woman's individualism is admired and loved, and their quirks accepted. And so I loved each character, but Miss Matty was certainly the star. As a whole, Cranford is a loving community, and I only wish there was more to read.<br /><br />I can understand how some feel uneasy about it's disjointedness, but if you read each chapter like a short story with the same characters it makes sense (though it is chronological). Cranford is a novel I will cherish and certainly read again. </span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_154862171">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154862171" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3144945-alex" class="left imgcol" title="Alex"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1303883046p2/3144945.jpg" alt="Alex" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/154862171?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3144945-alex" class="user" title="Alex">Alex</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6534328-cranford" title="Hardcover 9780141442549" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2011" class="actionLinkLite">2011</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=reading-through-history" class="actionLinkLite">reading-through-history</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=rth-lifetime" class="actionLinkLite">rth-lifetime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154862171">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6881171215608075020">Is it possible to discuss Cranford without using the word "charming?" It'd be like playing literary Taboo. Like trying to talk about <a title="The Road by Cormac McCarthy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6288.The_Road">The Road</a> without saying "bleak," or <a title="The Catcher in the Rye by J.D. Salinger" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5107.The_Catcher_in_the_Rye">Catcher in the Rye</a> without "insufferable twat."<br /><br />Cranford is a charming book. If it seems a bit more episodic than plot-driven, it's because it is; it was originally commissioned by Dickens as a series of eight essays for his publication <em>Household Works.</em> It was enormously popular, so Gaskell ended up novelizing it. And it does have</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6881171215608075020">Is it possible to discuss Cranford without using the word "charming?" It'd be like playing literary Taboo. Like trying to talk about <a title="The Road by Cormac McCarthy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6288.The_Road">The Road</a> without saying "bleak," or <a title="The Catcher in the Rye by J.D. Salinger" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5107.The_Catcher_in_the_Rye">Catcher in the Rye</a> without "insufferable twat."<br /><br />Cranford is a charming book. If it seems a bit more episodic than plot-driven, it's because it is; it was originally commissioned by Dickens as a series of eight essays for his publication <em>Household Works.</em> It was enormously popular, so Gaskell ended up novelizing it. And it does have a bit more plot than it's given credit for: it has a protagonist - Miss Matty - and an arc - her several swings in fortune. (And when I heard Dame Judi Dench had played Miss Matty for the BBC, my response was, "Well, of course she did." That was as inevitable as Patrick Stewart playing Professor X, or Ken Branagh frothing his way through King Lear in 2030.)<br /><br />It's also partly autobiographical; many of the most vivid scenes are from Gaskell's upbringing in the very similar town of Knutsford, and first appeared in her autobiographical essay <em>The Last Generation.</em> If the drop-dead hilarious story involving lace and pussies seems a bit out of place to you...it's too weird not to be true. Books that try to be funny rarely work for me; Cranford is a rare exception. I was entertained.<br /><br />There's some debate over whether Cranford is a feminist book or not. You could argue that it depicts a utopian society run by women (Amazons, even!) who take care of each other; and you could point to the narrator's detailed rundown of the things Miss Matty isn't qualified to do (Ch. XIV) as a critique of the lack of education available to women, which it is. Or you could call it a loving satire of a bunch of silly old ladies in bad hats. Charlotte Bronte - one of a circle of close, supportive female friends Gaskell created, which also included Florence Nightingale - wrote that <a title="William Makepeace Thackeray" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3953.William_Makepeace_Thackeray">William Thackeray</a> should take Cranford, "put himself to bed, and lie there...til he had learnt by diligent study how to be satirical without being exquisitely bitter." Both of those readings are accurate, and I think Cranford is as feminist as you want it to be, in the same way that 2 Live Crew are - or were - as nasty as they wanted to be, which in retrospect was more charming than nasty. <br /><br />And in fact both parties - Gaskell and 2 Live Crew - talked a great deal about pussies, though in different contexts.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6881171215608075020">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_179372895">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179372895" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2908629-ellie" class="left imgcol" title="Ellie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1399799985p2/2908629.jpg" alt="Ellie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/179372895?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2908629-ellie" class="user" title="Ellie">Ellie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/830128.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780192832092" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2908629-ellie?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2908629-ellie?shelf=victorian-victoriana" class="actionLinkLite">victorian-victoriana</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2908629-ellie?shelf=2011ind-chal200bks" class="actionLinkLite">2011ind-chal200bks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer179372895">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8358789263597352147"><a title="Cranford by Elizabeth Gaskell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/182381.Cranford">Cranford</a> by <a title="Elizabeth Gaskell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1413437.Elizabeth_Gaskell">Elizabeth Gaskell</a> is Victorian literature at its best. A small community-in this case, for some reason populated almost exclusively by women, in which all the events of the larger world occur (love, death, marriage, childbirth, financial struggles) but in microcosmically allowing their repercussions to reverberate more loudly while simultaneously being softened by the arch tone of the book and rather hilarious eccentricities of the town's inhabitants.<br /><br />I loved this book. I would avoid</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8358789263597352147"><a title="Cranford by Elizabeth Gaskell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/182381.Cranford">Cranford</a> by <a title="Elizabeth Gaskell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1413437.Elizabeth_Gaskell">Elizabeth Gaskell</a> is Victorian literature at its best. A small community-in this case, for some reason populated almost exclusively by women, in which all the events of the larger world occur (love, death, marriage, childbirth, financial struggles) but in microcosmically allowing their repercussions to reverberate more loudly while simultaneously being softened by the arch tone of the book and rather hilarious eccentricities of the town's inhabitants.<br /><br />I loved this book. I would avoid living there at all costs but I grew to love this town and the women who lived there. And while I laughed at there many foibles and their sometimes extreme ways of holding together their pride, I also began to feel protective of them.<br /><br />The story is a series of episodes that are loosely strung together, more by emotional relationships than by narrative connectivity. But it holds together well, the writing is crisp and clear and the world portrayed felt as vivid as the one surrounding me.<br /><br />I strongly recommend this book for people who enjoy entering a world and its relationships in which drama may be small but it is heartfelt.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8358789263597352147">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_96151148">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96151148" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1406509-laurel" class="left imgcol" title="Laurel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442531711p2/1406509.jpg" alt="Laurel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/96151148?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1406509-laurel" class="user" title="Laurel">Laurel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2184302.Cranford" title="Audiobook 9789626348505" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1406509-laurel?shelf=british-society" class="actionLinkLite">british-society</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1406509-laurel?shelf=victorian-era-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">victorian-era-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1406509-laurel?shelf=audio-books" class="actionLinkLite">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer96151148">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12322950225116039121">To prime myself for Return to Cranford, the new Masterpiece Classic sequel to last year’s award-winning mini-series Cranford on PBS, I wanted to read Mrs. Gaskell’s original novel that it was adapted from. Since I am always short of reading time, I chose instead to listen to an audio recording, my favorite pastime during my commute to work. After a bit of research on Cranford audio book recordings, I settled on the Naxos edition. From my experience with their recording of Jane Austen’s novels I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12322950225116039121">To prime myself for Return to Cranford, the new Masterpiece Classic sequel to last year’s award-winning mini-series Cranford on PBS, I wanted to read Mrs. Gaskell’s original novel that it was adapted from. Since I am always short of reading time, I chose instead to listen to an audio recording, my favorite pastime during my commute to work. After a bit of research on Cranford audio book recordings, I settled on the Naxos edition. From my experience with their recording of Jane Austen’s novels I knew the quality would be superior. I was not disappointed. <br /><br />A witty and poignant portrait of small town life in an early Victorian-era English village, <em>Cranford</em> was first published in 1851 as a serial in the magazine Household Words edited by Charles Dickens. Inspired by author Elizabeth Gaskell’s (1810-1865) early life in Knutsford in Cheshire where she was raised by an aunt after her mother’s death and father’s subsequent re-marriage, the novel revolves around the narrator Miss Mary Smith and the Amazons of the community: the authoritative Miss Deborah Jenkyns and her kindhearted but timid younger sister Matty, the always well informed Miss Miss Pole and the self-important aristocratic Mrs. Jamieson. This gentle satire of village life does not supply much of a plot – but amazingly it does not matter. Gaskell has the incredible talent of making everyday occurrences and life events totally engrossing. Miss Matty’s conservative friends, the middle-aged spinsters and widows of Cranford, do not want their quaint life and traditions altered one bit. They like Cranford just as it has always been, therefore when the industrial revolution that swept through England in the 1840’s encroaches upon their Shangri-La, they lament and bustle about attempting to do everything in there power to stop the evil railroad’s arrival. Gaskell is a deft tactician at dry humor, not unlike her predecessor Jane Austen, and the comedy in Cranford balanced with a bit of tragedy is its most endearing quality. <br /><br />This unabridged audio book recording is aptly read by Claire Willie whose sensitive and lyrical interpretation of Gaskell’s narrative enhanced my enjoyment of the story by two fold. Her rendering of the different characters with change of timbre and intonation was charmingly effective. My favorite character was of course the kindhearted Miss Matty. Even though she is of a certain age she has a child-like naïveté refreshingly seeing her friends and her world in simple terms. In opposition to our present day lives of cell-phones, blackberries and information overload, a trip to Cranford was a welcome respite. I recommend it highly. <br /><br />2010 marks the 200th anniversary of author Elizabeth Cleghorn Gaskell nee Stevenson’s birth on 29 September 1810 in Chelsea, which was then on the outskirts of London. In celebration of her bi-centenary, Naxos AudioBooks will be releasing three additional recordings of her novels: <em>North and South</em> in February again read by Claire Willis, <em>Wives and Daughters</em> in March read by Patience Tomlinson and <em>Cousin Phillis</em> in May read by Joe Marsh. Happily, I will be enjoying many hours of great Gaskell listening this year.<br /><br />Laurel Ann, Austenprose</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12322950225116039121">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/97963194?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 11, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/161559-arukiyomi" class="user" title="Arukiyomi">Arukiyomi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer97963194">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15333910160001435534">The 1001 Books list has totally changed the way I read novels. It’s given me access to writers that have deeply influenced the way I see the world and has given me memories of characters and storylines that have been incredibly powerful. And then it’s introduced me to Elizabeth Gaskell and the trivial wittering rubbish of Cranford.<br /><br />This is a book about absolutely nothing. I recently thought Northanger Abbey lacked any substance. How very wrong I was. Cranford redefines pointlessness. I waited in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15333910160001435534">The 1001 Books list has totally changed the way I read novels. It’s given me access to writers that have deeply influenced the way I see the world and has given me memories of characters and storylines that have been incredibly powerful. And then it’s introduced me to Elizabeth Gaskell and the trivial wittering rubbish of Cranford.<br /><br />This is a book about absolutely nothing. I recently thought Northanger Abbey lacked any substance. How very wrong I was. Cranford redefines pointlessness. I waited in vain for one significant thing to happen throughout the entire book and, when it finally did, the novel ended. It was an audio book and, for a minute, I thought my mp3 player had had a fit and I’d lost some files. But no, that was it.<br /><br />My mother in law asked me why it was so bad. To help her understand I asked her to imagine following a contemporary blog of some young 20-something whose life is filled with triviality, all of which she details every day. You meet her shallow friends with bland personalities, hear her discuss with avid attention for pages and pages things that shouldn’t justify a blink of attention. That’s Cranford, the petty ramblings of a young woman with nothing better to do. Even Wikipedia can’t come up with much on this one.<br /><br />I’m glad the reading’s over with… now I’ll just sit back and wait for the Gaskell-ites to comment and try to sell this one to me. Just go ahead and try, I dare you</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15333910160001435534">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_740800146">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/740800146" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/999171-anita" class="left imgcol" title="Anita"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1257827893p2/999171.jpg" alt="Anita" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/740800146?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/999171-anita" class="user" title="Anita">Anita</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer740800146">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5751917303674820822">Step away from Persuasion Austen lovers. Put down the 15th rereading of Pride and Prejudice. Jump ahead to a new century and read Cranford. This witty exploration of a sleepy English town where the women have a rigid caste system is lovingly and laughingly portrayed, and it will make your heart glad. You will love Miss Mattie and the others as they keep up conventions amidst flies in the system's ointment as people they love make poor decisions, i.e. marrying beneath them (or sometimes marrying</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5751917303674820822">Step away from Persuasion Austen lovers. Put down the 15th rereading of Pride and Prejudice. Jump ahead to a new century and read Cranford. This witty exploration of a sleepy English town where the women have a rigid caste system is lovingly and laughingly portrayed, and it will make your heart glad. You will love Miss Mattie and the others as they keep up conventions amidst flies in the system's ointment as people they love make poor decisions, i.e. marrying beneath them (or sometimes marrying at all), keeping up appearances when your money no longer fits your station, and what to serve at tea. The humor is gentle and Austenesque. There is no romantic love story or affair, just a little town that you would love to visit. And if you can't get enough, there is a PBS miniseries not to be missed--Cranford. With Judy Dench! What could be better? This book is free on Kindle and Nook--out of copyright. But wait, there's more. There is a sequel, Return to Cranford. I can't wait.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_841173941">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/841173941" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2272233-peggy" class="left imgcol" title="Peggy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1379120395p2/2272233.jpg" alt="Peggy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/841173941?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2272233-peggy" class="user" title="Peggy">Peggy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2272233-peggy?shelf=british" class="actionLinkLite">british</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer841173941">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13933586712081625455">Entertaining novel that depicts social relationships among the respectable classes in the early mid-nineteenth century. The first sentence drew me in completely, "In the first place, Cranford is in possession of the Amazons; all the holders of houses above a certain rent are women." Gaskell goes on to describe the genteel poverty of the town. The code of social conduct forbids its inhabitants to admit to their limited circumstances, so each pretends to be of more comfortable means, all the while</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13933586712081625455">Entertaining novel that depicts social relationships among the respectable classes in the early mid-nineteenth century. The first sentence drew me in completely, "In the first place, Cranford is in possession of the Amazons; all the holders of houses above a certain rent are women." Gaskell goes on to describe the genteel poverty of the town. The code of social conduct forbids its inhabitants to admit to their limited circumstances, so each pretends to be of more comfortable means, all the while knowing exactly where each stands in the social pecking order and why. The stories--the plot is episodic, with some stories extending over several chapters--revolve around Mattie Jenkyns, a middle-aged spinster who has been dominated life-long by her misguided and superior older sister Deborah. After Deborah dies, Mattie must navigate the world on her own. She is timid and sweet, yet has strong instincts towards justice. Mattie frets and worries over her own admirable behavior because it does not replicate that of her much admired older sister. The book is narrated by Miss Mattie's distant relative, a younger woman en route to her own spinsterhood. <em>Cranford </em> is a gentle comedy of manners that has less of an edge than Jane Austen's novels, which were popular at the time Gaskell was writing. The BBC series by the same name follows the book closely. <br /><br />I read this in a 1954 edition published by Everyman's Library. The book was small and light with thick, creamy pages. The typography of the edition used a ligature between all st combinations, which was distracting at first, but later became part of the charm of the reading experience. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13933586712081625455">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1151710833">

  <a href="/user/show/4814165-bob-arnold" class="left imgcol" title="Bob Arnold"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295123458p2/4814165.jpg" alt="Bob Arnold" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1151710833?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4814165-bob-arnold" class="user" title="Bob Arnold">Bob Arnold</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4814165-bob-arnold?shelf=ebooks" class="actionLinkLite">ebooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4814165-bob-arnold?shelf=19th-century-classics" class="actionLinkLite">19th-century-classics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1151710833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer987460977356768593">I ended up liking this much better than I thought I would. At first I was lost as to how all the characters fit together. It felt like walking into a room full of people not knowing anyone. In addition to not knowing anyone in the room nobody acknowledges my presence. I'm in the middle of a conversation not knowing anything about the lives of people around me. I found it daunting getting up to speed on the life and times of the people of Cranford. I even considered abandoning it. I am glad I was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText987460977356768593">I ended up liking this much better than I thought I would. At first I was lost as to how all the characters fit together. It felt like walking into a room full of people not knowing anyone. In addition to not knowing anyone in the room nobody acknowledges my presence. I'm in the middle of a conversation not knowing anything about the lives of people around me. I found it daunting getting up to speed on the life and times of the people of Cranford. I even considered abandoning it. I am glad I was patient and stuck with to the end. It was the humor that kept me going until I caught up with the characters and their relationship to one another. Most of the humor is subtle, involving gossip about other people in the community.<br /><br />One of the things I found funny involved a cat and a piece of lace. During one of the many conversations between the women of Cranford, one lady commented to another about how beautiful a piece of lace she was wearing was. The owner of the lace thanked the other for the kind comment and acknowledged that it was indeed one of the most beautiful pieces of lace she had ever owned. Then the possessor of this magnificent piece of cloth told the story of how she almost lost this wondrous possession. Apparently one excellent way of cleaning and caring for this wonder cloth is to clean it with milk. <br /><br />One particular day after this lace was nicely cleaned at the milk bath spa it was laid out to dry. This is where the cat comes in. Old puss eats it, that’s right gobbled it up, gone. After several attempts fail to retrieve said lace from the front end of the cat, the owner of the lace and apparently owner of the cat too, for they seemed to be on friendly terms, except for this one incident, gives the cat something to drink. After all after all that lace, not to mention fingers down his throat, old puss is quite thirsty. <br /><br />This mystery concoction that old puss is forced to drink does indeed result in the reappearance of the lace. The lace survives and is still thought of as wondrous. The dishonorable cat also survived, hopefully wiser for the experience. Now the ladies listening to this story are all joyously happy that the lace and the cat survived. However, none of the ladies seemed curious about which end of the cat the lace reappeared. Me I’m still curious about it, whatever end old puss returned his ill-gotten gains I think the ladies were very polite and proper by not mentioning it. What else can you expect from the gentile ladies of Cranford.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="987460977356768593">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_33340018">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33340018" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/305104-diana" class="left imgcol" title="Diana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1304051266p2/305104.jpg" alt="Diana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/33340018?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/305104-diana" class="user" title="Diana">Diana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Diana by: </span>
      The BBC
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/305104-diana?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/305104-diana?shelf=feminism" class="actionLinkLite">feminism</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/305104-diana?shelf=victorian" class="actionLinkLite">victorian</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/305104-diana?shelf=own-it" class="actionLinkLite">own-it</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/305104-diana?shelf=british" class="actionLinkLite">british</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer33340018">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4533340909204674574">After wading my way through a few duds, I was thrilled to read a true gem. I tried reading this once before. However, I was expecting a linear narrative and was therefore unprepared for this anecdotal novel. After watching the BBC miniseries (which, by the way, was excellent), I had a better idea of what to expect. <br /><br />Prior to 'Cranford' my only experience with Elizabeth Gaskell was 'North and South.' Although 'North and South' is undoubtedly one of my favorite books, as a novel littered by death i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4533340909204674574">After wading my way through a few duds, I was thrilled to read a true gem. I tried reading this once before. However, I was expecting a linear narrative and was therefore unprepared for this anecdotal novel. After watching the BBC miniseries (which, by the way, was excellent), I had a better idea of what to expect. <br /><br />Prior to 'Cranford' my only experience with Elizabeth Gaskell was 'North and South.' Although 'North and South' is undoubtedly one of my favorite books, as a novel littered by death it can be a bit heavy. Consequently, I was blown away by how well Gaskell wrote a humorous tale. At certain points, I was unable to stop my laughter. There are several characters who make you smile while simultaneously warming your heart. <br /><br />While 'Cranford' may, at first glance, seem to be about nothing, Gaskell has done something quite groundbreaking with this novel. As a town where its chief members are middle-class, single women who have little regard for the goings-on outside their insulated community, Cranford is almost matriarchal. And when compared with the world outside, Gaskell clearly suggests it is not Cranford that is to be found wanting. In fact, the way in which she highlights the lives of single women in the Victorian period is quite brilliant. Women who seem to be old-fashioned snobs prove to be strong, compassionate, caring, and self-sufficient. Witnessing the way in which these women cared for each other made me quite emotional.<br /><br />Overall, 'Cranford' is a delightful place to visit, and I was sad when forced to leave. Having been enchanted by both 'Cranford' and 'North and South', I am eager to further acquaint myself with this amazing author. (First reading: September 2009) <br /><br />I am thrilled to find Gaskell's novel just as charming the second time around. I will always treasure the time I have spent in Cranford -- and look forward to future visits. I feel confident they will be many. (Second reading: 20 February 2012)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4533340909204674574">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/6970638-sheri" class="user" title="Sheri">Sheri</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6970638-sheri?shelf=poverty-class-issues" class="actionLinkLite">poverty-class-issues</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6970638-sheri?shelf=male-female-power-sex-attractivenes" class="actionLinkLite">male-female-power-sex-attractivenes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1198880468">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4330677822675639781">I liked it, but I liked Mary Barton better. As others have remarked, rather than a novel it is really a set of vignettes about the women of Cranford.<br /><br />I was not sure about the characterization of Cranford as Amazonian; while the male characters are not sufficiently important, they do exist. The focus was on female society and several comments about the superiority of spinsterhood are unusual ("A man....is so in the way in the house" and "although she would have despised the modern idea of women be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4330677822675639781">I liked it, but I liked Mary Barton better. As others have remarked, rather than a novel it is really a set of vignettes about the women of Cranford.<br /><br />I was not sure about the characterization of Cranford as Amazonian; while the male characters are not sufficiently important, they do exist. The focus was on female society and several comments about the superiority of spinsterhood are unusual ("A man....is so in the way in the house" and "although she would have despised the modern idea of women being equal to men. Equal indeed! she knew they were superior"), but there are men that play solid roles: Captain Brown, Mr. Holbrook, Mr. Hoggins, and Peter. <br /><br />I was also unsure about the relative poverty of the characters. The members of Cranford society are not rich, but they are certainly not poor. They all have at least one servant and no real occupation (they live off their capital). When Miss Matty loses her capital, they are all able to help her (including the servant Martha) until Peter comes to the rescue. These are certainly not rich folks, but despite frequent comments to this effect they are not poverty stricken either. <br /><br />Gaskell's commentary is quite witty and enjoyable throughout. She is very straight-faced and ironic when she describes ridiculous rituals or perspectives of the ladies.<br /><br />Overall it is a good period piece and definitely ahead of its time for feminist perspective.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4330677822675639781">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1196002991">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196002991" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3668593-marita" class="left imgcol" title="Marita"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Marita" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1196002991?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3668593-marita" class="user" title="Marita">Marita</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer1196002991'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1196002991">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2101112070568555896">"No man is a failure who has friends." Probably because I just watched <em>It's a Wonderful Life</em> this quote from Clarence came to mind as I finished <em>Cranford</em>.<br /><br /> I don't often recommend or enjoy watching a movie version of a book before reading it, but this is one of the rare cases where I feel that my enjoyment of the book was enhanced by seeing the movie first. I loved picturing Imelda Staunton with that solitary feather bobbing every which way in her hat as she went about Cranford, agitated with exc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2101112070568555896">"No man is a failure who has friends." Probably because I just watched <em>It's a Wonderful Life</em> this quote from Clarence came to mind as I finished <em>Cranford</em>.<br /><br /> I don't often recommend or enjoy watching a movie version of a book before reading it, but this is one of the rare cases where I feel that my enjoyment of the book was enhanced by seeing the movie first. I loved picturing Imelda Staunton with that solitary feather bobbing every which way in her hat as she went about Cranford, agitated with excitement over some sensational bit of news to share with her neighbors. I loved picturing Dame Judi Dench as the gentle and excessively humble Miss Matty.<br /><br />This is a beautiful story of friendship and community. I loved the stories about everyday life in the quaint British town of Cranford. Some may find descriptions like this boring or tedious, but I love them for their window into what everyday life was like at that time, and because I believe that it's those moments of everydayness where real community happens.<br /><br />The idea of old-fashioned community is fascinating to me because it seems sometimes like it is a thing of the past. The way this band of women revelled in visiting with each other, playing cards by the fire, sharing secrets and town news, faced hardship together and took care of each other in times of sadness and hardship was beautiful to me. Nowadays women meet for lunch at a restaurant or have coffee at Starbucks, which is great. But there is a particular kind of intimacy that is lost in not meeting in each other's homes. Even though I've never experienced a small town such as Cranford, I found myself nostalgic for places like a general store, post office or even the city streets where people would naturally congregate on a day-to-day basis. <br /><br />This book is almost a collection of recollections of the narrator rather than a true novel, and the story that affected me the most was when Miss Matty finds herself in vastly reduced circumstances and faces being destitute. When her friends find out, they each give her a certain amount of money according to their means to help Miss Matty, but without her ever finding out about it. Much like the community in <em>It's a Wonderful Life</em>, the town of Cranford rally around Miss Matty and find sly and secret ways to help her.<br /><br />I love this book and its characters and feel that this is a book I will want to revisit many times.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2101112070568555896">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_173407299">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173407299" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2986995-mary-ronan-drew" class="left imgcol" title="Mary Ronan Drew"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1302365296p2/2986995.jpg" alt="Mary Ronan Drew" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/173407299?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2986995-mary-ronan-drew" class="user" title="Mary Ronan Drew">Mary Ronan Drew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2986995-mary-ronan-drew?shelf=kindle" class="actionLinkLite">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173407299">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11577276805933225471">Mrs Gaskell is making a comeback. And not just with my online Trollope group, which has been reading Cranford recently and comparing – or rather, contrasting – it with Trollope’s novels. Libraries are acquiring her novels, many are on the shelves of bookstores, and all are easily available through amazon.com. The BBC has produced excellent, and very popular, made-for-TV series of Cranford, North and South, and Wives and Daughters. My alerts with Google and the NY Times pop up with Gaskell as oft</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11577276805933225471">Mrs Gaskell is making a comeback. And not just with my online Trollope group, which has been reading Cranford recently and comparing – or rather, contrasting – it with Trollope’s novels. Libraries are acquiring her novels, many are on the shelves of bookstores, and all are easily available through amazon.com. The BBC has produced excellent, and very popular, made-for-TV series of Cranford, North and South, and Wives and Daughters. My alerts with Google and the NY Times pop up with Gaskell as often as with Trollope. Two hundred years after her birth she is more popular than she has ever been.<br /><br />She made her name with Cranford, published in Dickens’ Household Words from 1851 to 1853 and the book remains her most beloved. Based on the town of Knutsford where Gaskell lived with an aunt when she was a child, Cranford is near a big city, Drumble, a stand-in for Manchester, where Gaskell lived for most of her adult life with her husband, a Unitarian minister.<br /><br />The latest BBC series – there are actually two series – are a combination of Cranford, My Lady Ludlow, and Mr Harrison’s Confessions. The TV version of the story very different from that in the book, which is a cozy episodic collection of stories with a thin plot and much humor. For lovers of Victorian fiction Elizabeth Gaskell is a must-read author. And if you fall for her as I have done, Jenny Uglow has written a fine biography.<br /><br />The house in which she lived with her husband still stands. <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.elizabethgaskellhouse.org/" target="_blank">http://www.elizabethgaskellhouse.org/</a> Unfortunately, after years of fund-raising and restoration thieves recently stole the roof for the lead and costs for a new roof and repair of water damage are significant.<br /><br />2011 No 86 <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11577276805933225471">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>
