          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christopher by: </span>
      lonebearimages@gmail.com
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=british-literature" class="actionLinkLite">british-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=victorian-literature" class="actionLinkLite">victorian-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=read-in-2010" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=author-elizabeth-gaskell" class="actionLinkLite">author-elizabeth-gaskell</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=short-story-novella-collections" class="actionLinkLite">short-story-novella-collections</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2482609-christopher-h?shelf=my-western-canon" class="actionLinkLite">my-western-canon</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer61989344">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2868503171580535559">I finished this book this morning on the train on my way to work. What a sweet, elegant, witty, and gentle little book this is. <em>Cranford</em> is really a series of quasi-connected vignettes involving a group of spinster women in a quiet little town in the south of England. Each of the tales is full of little details about the little things, even bordering on minutiae, that are so important to a group of very close friends. There are laugh-out-loud funny moments, and there are poignant, even sad, mome</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2868503171580535559">I finished this book this morning on the train on my way to work. What a sweet, elegant, witty, and gentle little book this is. <em>Cranford</em> is really a series of quasi-connected vignettes involving a group of spinster women in a quiet little town in the south of England. Each of the tales is full of little details about the little things, even bordering on minutiae, that are so important to a group of very close friends. There are laugh-out-loud funny moments, and there are poignant, even sad, moments too. <br /><br />Now I know why people are eager to see a similarity in some of Elizabeth Gaskell's writing to that of Jane Austen. I saw touches of this in Gaskell's <em>Wives and Daughters</em>, but it is much, much more evident in this book. Also, for those interested in the fashions and dressing habits of women in the 1830s through the 1850s, this is the book for you. One of the appendices in the back is wholly devoted to the women's fashions of the time of <em>Cranford</em> with wonderful illustrations.<br /><br />When you are looking for some peace and quiet, and the ability to sit back and smile and chuckle to yourself, pick up a copy of <em>Cranford</em>. I think this would make a terrific book for a bookclub to jointly read and discuss. I highly recommend this book!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2868503171580535559">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/166022721?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2189910-whitney" class="user" title="Whitney ">Whitney </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6534328-cranford" title="Hardcover 9780141442549" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2189910-whitney?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2189910-whitney?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer166022721">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6764915246875258616">Cranford by Elizabeth Gaskell is a collection of short stories surrounding the small town of Cranford and the eccentric women who live there.<br /><br />As I said, Cranford is a small town which is high in the population of female. In the first section of the book, every male who enters the town drops like flies making it feel jinxed or like an old fashioned sorority.<br /><br /> Elizabeth Gaskell's novel is a sequence of short stories that all intertwine. I'm typically not a short story reader so it took me a while to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6764915246875258616">Cranford by Elizabeth Gaskell is a collection of short stories surrounding the small town of Cranford and the eccentric women who live there.<br /><br />As I said, Cranford is a small town which is high in the population of female. In the first section of the book, every male who enters the town drops like flies making it feel jinxed or like an old fashioned sorority.<br /><br /> Elizabeth Gaskell's novel is a sequence of short stories that all intertwine. I'm typically not a short story reader so it took me a while to get into it and go with the flow. Although, once there Cranford is enchanting! All the characters are so lively that one can not help but fall in love, which is odd because most of the females are against that.<br /><br />You cannot write a review without speaking of Miss Matty. She is a kind old soul who while should seem a woman with much wisdom, she is in fact a nieve child-like girl who everyone coddles and adores because of her sweet nature. I won't say much in fear that I could give too much away, but an example of this is when Matty's companion is engaged to be married but worries about mentioning it in case it were to upset her and devises a plan so everything benefits the surrounding persons.<br /><br />My favorite and what I felt to be the most entertaining stories is of Lady Glenmire's appearance. Believed to be the highest of society with the residence in town all in a tizzy over the preparations only to find that she is no different from themselves. <br /><br />The running around reminded me of a Faulty Towers episode particularly the one where "The Germans" visit the hotel. Really, when I think about it the majority of these stories could have been a highly sophisticated Faulty Towers. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6764915246875258616">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_783047183">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/783047183" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10661959-ali-nazifpour" class="left imgcol" title="Ali Nazifpour"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1341333834p2/10661959.jpg" alt="Ali Nazifpour" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/783047183?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 10, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10661959-ali-nazifpour" class="user" title="Ali Nazifpour">Ali Nazifpour</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14575500-cranford" title="Paperback 9781908533449" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer783047183">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14062952816665230407">To describe this novel in one expression, one can call it "true to life". It is one of the most realistic novels I've read, and I mean the word in its strictest sense. The tone of the narrator is seamless and natural, as if she really is talking to you, and the episodic nature of the novel reinforces the effect that you are listening to a woman in person who has taken your hand and is walking you through the memory lane. The characters of the novel are not larger than life and they do not touch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14062952816665230407">To describe this novel in one expression, one can call it "true to life". It is one of the most realistic novels I've read, and I mean the word in its strictest sense. The tone of the narrator is seamless and natural, as if she really is talking to you, and the episodic nature of the novel reinforces the effect that you are listening to a woman in person who has taken your hand and is walking you through the memory lane. The characters of the novel are not larger than life and they do not touch grand concepts of humanity, they are not epic heroes nor evil villains, they feel like ordinary people, no more and no less, and you get to know them and get used to them like you know your own relatives. Few, if any, extraordinary events happen during the novel, and the ultimate plot that ties all the episodes together is as bare as life itself, not characterized by the rise and climax and fall of dramatic points but the passage of time.<br /><br />However, this extremist realism doesn't turn the novel into a boring read or a pointless account of lives. What truly distinguishes this novel from the boring nature of the ordinary life is Gaskell's skill as a great author. We read on because the characters are fascinating in their common nature, and we eventually fall in love with them with all their flaws. Gaskell's handling of her Amazonian cast is humorous and sharp in its criticism, and yet the criticism is loving and gentle at its heart. And the book manages to capture a complete picture of the society it pictures and the women who lived in it.<br /><br />Such a book could end up very badly. But it didn't. Like its characters and its world, <em>Cranford</em> is a modest masterpiece. But it is one, unmistakeably.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14062952816665230407">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_451315190">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451315190" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9255064-melissa" class="left imgcol" title="Melissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1343822200p2/9255064.jpg" alt="Melissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/451315190?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9255064-melissa" class="user" title="Melissa">Melissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/182381.Cranford" title="Paperback 9780141439884" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer451315190">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14955998851648306845">I didn't love Cranford at first. It felt trivial and slow. But half way through the book I realized that I loved these characters, our narrator Miss Smith, the gossipy Miss Pole and most of all, the gentle, trusting Miss Matty. <br /><br />The book is made up of 16 chapters; each chronicles a small event in the quiet English town of Cranford in the 1840s. The women in the town are a tight-knit group, skeptical of outsiders and protective of each other. There are many humorous sections with mistaken identiti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14955998851648306845">I didn't love Cranford at first. It felt trivial and slow. But half way through the book I realized that I loved these characters, our narrator Miss Smith, the gossipy Miss Pole and most of all, the gentle, trusting Miss Matty. <br /><br />The book is made up of 16 chapters; each chronicles a small event in the quiet English town of Cranford in the 1840s. The women in the town are a tight-knit group, skeptical of outsiders and protective of each other. There are many humorous sections with mistaken identities, misunderstandings and unneeded panic, but those aren't the sections that will stay with me in years to come. <br /><br />The chapter that finally hooked me was ch. 13 Stopped Payment. When a local bank has unexpected troubles we have a chance to see Miss Matty's goodness shine. She is so selfless in her concern for others that it broke my heart. Her sincere love for her friends and neighbors knows no bounds. When Miss Matty own finances seem dire, the dear ladies of Cranford come together to help her without her knowledge. That's the true heart of this sweet book, friendship that rises to the occasion, silently offering a shoulder to cry on or a hand to hold. <br /><br />To me, this quote from Miss Pole summed up how the women of Cranford see themselves ... <br /><br />"We, the ladies of Cranford, in my drawing-room assembled, can resolve upon something. I imagine we are none of us what may be called rich, though we all posses a genteel competency, sufficient for taste that are elegant and refined, and would not, if they could, be vulgarly ostentatious."</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14955998851648306845">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1382458091">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1382458091" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11258836-elinor" class="left imgcol" title="Elinor"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442951555p2/11258836.jpg" alt="Elinor" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1382458091?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11258836-elinor" class="user" title="Elinor">Elinor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9514020-cranford" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1382458091">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9787474470688694129">I can find no fault in this book. Each character is finely drawn, the plot is a simple yet effective framework for the characters, and the setting -- a quiet English country village, just before the Industrial Revolution -- is quite perfect. I love the way these fictional people (can they really be made up?) think and speak and behave. Unless you demand more sound and fury in your novels, this is a deeply satisfying read. I downloaded it for free from the Project Gutenberg website.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nRsbi1U/tXRciVwDlnMnVdtisLytQJTt2mMi78pxP7n4zyRYp+2hjtBRKLjoEsHnkpVzpeSd00ewaid9BuTJ/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Written&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText13861260656346723697\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;In 1834, Charlotte Bronte, together with her brother Branwell, created the imaginary kingdom of Angria, about which she was to write prolifically for the next five years. The five “novelettes” in this volume are the last of her Angrian tales. Written from the viewpoint of the cynical, gossipy Charles Townshend, they offer an ironic portrait of the intrigues, scandals, and passions of an aristocratic beau monde. With their varied cast of characters, the stories provide a fascinating glimpse into the mind and creative processes of the young writer who was to become one of the world’s greatest Disinherited by law and brutally ousted from Combe-Raven, the idyllic country estate which has been their peaceful home since childhood, the two young women are left to fend for themselves. While the submissive Norah follows a path of duty and hardship as a governess, her high-spirited and rebellious younger sister has made other decisions. Determined to regain her rightful inheritance at any cost, Magdalen uses her unconventional beauty and dramatic talent in recklessly pursuing her revenge. Aided by the audacious swindler Captain Wragge, she braves a series of trials leading up to the climactic test: can she trade herself in marriage to the man she loathes?\n\nWritten in the early 1860s, between The Woman in White and The Moonstone, No Name was rejected as immoral by critics of its time, but is today regarded as a novel of outstanding social insight, showing Collins at the height of     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1413437.Elizabeth_Gaskell">About Elizabeth Gaskell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1413437.Elizabeth_Gaskell"><img alt="1413437" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1223499865p2/1413437.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16183723706933162943"><strong>Elizabeth Cleghorn Gaskell</strong>, née Stevenson (29 September 1810 – 12 November 1865), often referred to simply as Mrs. Gaskell, was an English novelist and short story writer during the Victorian era. She is perhaps best known for her biography of Charlotte Brontë. Her novels offer a detailed portrait of the lives of many strata of society, including the very poor, and as such are of interest to socia</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16183723706933162943"><strong>Elizabeth Cleghorn Gaskell</strong>, née Stevenson (29 September 1810 – 12 November 1865), often referred to simply as Mrs. Gaskell, was an English novelist and short story writer during the Victorian era. She is perhaps best known for her biography of Charlotte Brontë. Her novels offer a detailed portrait of the lives of many strata of society, including the very poor, and as such are of interest to social historians as well as lovers of literature.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16183723706933162943">...more</a>
